Even with flexeril (muscle relaxant), tramadol (narcotic pain med), and ibuprofen 600mg (pain med and anti-inflammatory), the pain going down my right leg was unbearable, to the point where I could not walk or drive properly. I also explained to her that I have been seeing a physical therapist regularly to solve the root cause of my pain. Karen recommended I receive a steroid and toradol shot. I did not want injectable therapy, and asked for gabapentin instead to help with the nerve pain. She would not prescribe me gabapentin but insisted on steroid therapy with a toradol shot. I asked her why she was uncomfortable with gabapentin, as it is recommended in clinical guidelines for neuropathic pain, even in acute settings such as post-operative pain. She told me that gabapentin will not solve the core of the problem. I understood where she was coming from, but I felt that she was not understanding the pain that I am going through, which was the excruciating nerve pain going down my leg. I still needed something to help curb my nerve pain, which is what gabapentin targets.

As a clinician myself with training in an acute care hospital, it‚Äôs disturbing that PA Karen would lean to injectable steroids and toradol as her first line of therapy. I even pulled up data from clinical trials and Lexicomp (clinical database), and there was an abundance of clinical data that supports the use of gabapentin for acute neuropathic pain. I tried to show PA Karen this data that I was able to find,  but she dismissed me saying if I want a second opinion, to go somewhere else.

Please try to view this from a patient‚Äôs experience, who took the time to go to this urgent care, in a lot of pain, and then to be told to go somewhere else because the PA doesn‚Äôt want to prescribe a med that I need. It‚Äôs a med that is indicated for my condition, not a controlled substance, and something that the patient personally prefers and is much safer than jumping the gun with injectable steroid therapy.

I eventually spoke to an administrator, who recommended for me to go to their other urgent care.

Overall, as a patient of this clinic and a clinician myself, I was very disappointed and disturbed by the care I received. I understand that a clinician should never prescribe or do something they are uncomfortable with, but to insist on avoiding APPROPRIATE therapy for the patient is absolutely ridiculous. The PA was rejecting evidence based medicine. That is just terrible...!!! In addition, to tell a patient who is in pain and had a long struggle to even get to the clinic itself was very hurtful and disappointing.

I highly recommend you avoid this urgent  care and seek clinical help elsewhere..< /review>
